text:
This is seriously an epically awesome cake! It's easy to make, and one of those recipes that make people think you put 100x more work into it than you actually did. Quick to put together, and tastes amazing. It's also a very forgiving recipe, as I didn't follow it to a T and was still wonderful. Didn't want to spend 8 dollars for a teaspoon of instant coffee, so I skipped it altogether. Poured about 1/4 cup of coffee into the cake mix, and doubled all of the kahlua measurements. (4 table spoons instead of 2 in ALL parts where kahlua was required). The next time I make it, I might use 3/4 cup of coffee drizzle instead of 1/2, as some of it inevitably falls off he edges. Regardless, this cake barely lasted a day in the house. Light, airy, easy. Definitely would make again!

text:
This was an experiment as I'd never made tiramisu before...and it turned out amazing!  Definitely some things to learn...but the main thing is that I had to beat the frosting for 11 minutes before it was a consistency to spread, so don't stop mixing too soon.  I also folded in about a cup of the filling with the frosting prior to decorating the cake :)...and, as mentioned in a previous review, I didn't use any liqueur in the frosting  but used about a T of instant coffee powder instead.  I had tried, and failed, with the additional liquid of the liqueur and it turned out awful.  I, also, did two layers coffee mixture and only one white cake layer.  This is going to be in high demand from my friends :)

text:
Oh, holy cow was this good. I did as other reviewers stated and made 2 coffee layers of cake. Doubled the instant coffee and added an extra tablespoon on liquor wherever it was called for. The cake is light as air, looks super impressive, and tastes phenomenal. I had a little trouble with the filling being a little runny and leaking out of the sides. I may have over mixed it, or the extra coffee liquor may have liquified it too much. I found throwing it in the freezer for 10 min or so did the trick to set it. I frosted it, sprinkled with cocoa, added the chocolate curls, and let it sit overnight in the fridge. The guests were wowed, definitely a keeper!

Having never tried any type of tiramisu prior I'm glad this cake was my first! It was totally delicious and my guests loved it too! I opted to make a 2 layer cake, as some others had suggested. Also, I used the mascarpone substitute since I'm not overly fond of an overly cheesy dessert.  I had absolutely no problems making this cake. Next time I make it I'll definitely cut the filling ingredients in half; I had a lot left over because I made a two layer instead. Like many others have recommended, make the cake the night before you want to serve it. The icing will settle beautifully overnight. What an awesome cake!!

text:
I tried this recipe and then made some changes to make it heavenly cake! 1. I used 8 inch pans to make the layers a little thicker and made 2 layers with coffee (mixed 2 tablespoons of instant coffee) 2. I used Amaretto insteaad of the coffee liquer - using anything else just doesn't make sense if you want to call it "Tiramisu". I added a generous amount, making sure that you can taste it but it's not an overwhelming (and very alcoholic) taste. You can use the cheapest Amaretto you can find and you won't notice any difference in taste. 3. I used double the amount of mascarpone - again, a MUST ingredient of Tiramisu. Any reviewer suggesting that cream cheese will taste just as good must not appreciate the unique taste of a true Tiramisu.  Thank you for a great recipe to start off with. It is now a favorite in our family and our group of friends!

text:
Cake was excellent, very light. I divided the cake mix into thirds using my scale, and made 2/3 of the cake with coffee instead of water as called for in the recipe. That dissolved the granules much better! Used M84Michael's review for frosting-- "level 6 for the first 3 minutes then level 8 for 2 minutes in a cold kitchen aid mixer." It was perfect! I don't think the pirouettes were worth the money. The cake is pretty without them if frosted immediately. Plus the cake gets better over time, while the pirouettes just get soggy! If you do use pirouettes, you need two canisters, or to cut the pirouettes in half, which will be a little shorter than the cake.

This is the most AMAZING dessert.  You get the great Tiramisu taste b/c of the delicious filling and you also get your cake fix.  I did make some changes. I used Kahlua and coffee to drizzle over the cake and I also put some Kahlua in the cheese filling.  I also used yellow cake mix instead of the white.  I generally prefer the yellow to white.  Seriously, you have to make this cake.  Next birthday that we celebrate (mine in August!), we will definitely be having this cake.

YUM!  I agree with another reviewer - this is an extremely forgiving recipe.  I messed up and added the 1/4 C. of coffee and 1 T. of coffee liquor to the cake batter by accident (oops!).  I feared it would never get done in the center - but it did!... and this cake turned out phenomenal.  I also doubled all the liquor throughout the recipe (AND doubled the instant coffee) (and I didn't remove any other ingredients), and this was so great tasting.  Lots of coffee taste, very moist and fabulous.  Also looked so professional on the plate when sprinkled with cocoa powder and chocolate curls.

text:
I dissolved the coffee in 2 Tbsp. hot water before mixing into the batter. The white layers create a beautiful contrast with very dark streaks of coffee on their tops, so I would stick to two white layers and only one coffee layer to keep the deep contrast. I like tiramisu, but I like that this recipe is a unique cake instead, so I stayed with the recipe amounts instead of making the layers overly moist. I followed another cook's idea and used a spay bottle.
This recipe is a fantastic concept, but do use a homemade white cake if you have it in you. Even the strong flavor of coffee did not cover up the artificial taste and "lightness" of the cake mix.

text:
I made this cake for my best friend's birthday. She doesn't like traditional cake, so I picked something a little different. She and my friends all LOVED the cake (my boyfriend was a bit jealous I didn't make it for HIS birthday). My best friend's boyfriend even asked me where I bought the cake!

I followed all the tips above, like making two coffee-flavored layers instead of just one, and doubling the Kahlua, and using the substitute for Mascarpone cheese. 

One note: The recipe above from HEIDI8803 for the Mascarpone cheese substitute should be halved; the recipe it came from, the raspberry cheesecake, calls for 16 oz. of the cheese. 

The only problems I had with the recipe were my own fault; DO NOT let the frosting sit (probably common sense, but this was my first solo cake baking venture). Whip it up right before you are going to frost the cake, otherwise it will separate. Also, freeze the chocolate before you try to make the pretty chocolate curls, otherwise they are more like chocolate chunks. It still looked alright though.

Ditto everyone else's reviews.  This cake was absolutely delicious, and beautiful.  I made it for my husband's birthday, and it impressed everyone.  It's the first birthday cake that was completely gone - you know how most people take a few bites, or the health conscious bypass the birthday cake?  Nope, this one was fought over. text:
After making this several times following the recipe (still very good) I wanted to start customizing. Made cake from scratch using Cake Boss vanilla cake recipe. I doubled the filling for thicker layers, made 50% more of the frosting for thicker coverage, I doubled the coffee soak and  I added an extra tbs of coffee liqueur where called for. I find it tastes better if you let the cake soak at least 24 hrs. If time allows, also wait to make and frost the cake until 12 hours or less before serving. The whipped cream frosting will look fresh.

text:
This cake was delicious, even though I screwed up!  You can't beat a recipe that succeeds even when the cook fails.  I used Medaglia d'oro instant espresso coffee I found in Whole Foods for the middle cake layer. The problem was that I read "1/4 cup of instant coffee" instead of 1 tsp. (I was looking at the item below it) and as soon as I mixed the 1/4 cup into the cake layer I knew it was wrong.  I tasted the batter and thought for sure I had ruined it, but since I was without a car and without another cake mix, I proceeded to fix the cake completely.  It chilled and I served it to my husband for our anniversary.  I was very skeptical.  But it turned out fantastic.  We both loved it.  This is the way to go if you want more coffee flavor (next time I will probably use less than 1/4 cup of instant coffee, but definitely double the coffee/kahlua drizzle mixture.)     I used the mascarpone cheese, whipped the heavy cream for close to 6 or 7 minutes and got filling and frosting that was not runny at all.  Try this recipe.  You will love it.

Rave reviews! Everyone (21+) loves it! I have never had such a reaction from a cake before, well that's because this isn't your average cake. I am deliciosuly musing over the idea of having it be a layer of my wedding cake, yeah it is that good! I did use a little more Kahlua than the recipe stated, i eyeballed it and went my taste. I also made a little extra frosting and folded it into the mascarpone filling layer (about 1/2 cup) Also, I put some kahlua into the layer that has the instant coffee before baking. It made the middle layer much darker! Fantastic! Instead of chocolate curls on top I sprinkled the cake with crumbled health toffee bar. After chilling for a bit, the toffee gets soft and so so yummy! One Tip: This cake should not be eaten immediately, it does need to be chilled, preferably overnight. It tastes best that way.

text:
I'm not a regular baker, but this one was pretty easy to do.  My 12 yr old son and I breezed through this in under 90 minutes complete - plus we made the white cake mix from scratch - not a mix, too. So for people who say it's a bit hard, come on!  Cake was delicious, not too sweet and had a great texture.  Would like to try the mayo trick next time and definitely more coffee mixture (I used Tia Maria and some Starbucks, not Kahlua).  To get the big curls of chocolate, you really need more than those little baker's squares - so get yourself a big honking Hershey's or whatever.  Also, bake time was closer to the 20 minutes than the 25 (although ours was not a packaged mix).  Any longer than 22 minutes and we would have had a very dry cake.  Mayo is probably a great idea.  Used a pastry bag and some of the frosting to put a nice edge on the top and bottom of the cake - was easy and made it look pretty good, too.  Will make again very, very soon.

text:
This looks and tastes great.  I baked the Heavenly White Cake from this site as my base, and used 1 tsp. of instant espresso for the coffee layer.  I doubled the brewed coffee/liqueur mixture as suggested by others.  For the filling I used 12 oz. of mascarpone, 3T. of liqueur, 6 T. of sugar and forgot to mix in the whipped cream.  I assembled the cake 8 hours in advance and frosted with the whipped cream an hour before serving.  If you have access to mascarpone do use it; the texture and delicate flavour can't be duplicated with cream cheese.

text:
This was tasty and an impressive dessert to serve. I made it two times in the last week -- here are my lessons learned. I'm new to making layer cakes so this might be more helpful for a novice like myself instead of a seasoned pro. 

Both times I made the cake, I made the layers ahead of time, added the liquid (coffee+liquor) and froze it. That worked well for me -- it was easier to frost and I didn't worry about the cake crumbling.  Also both times I made the cake, I doubled the coffee and liquor as others have suggested. The flavor was just right for me.  I found marscapone at Walmart for $2.99 (it was in a case by the deli and take and bake pizzas). 

The first time I made the cake, I made it for my gender reveal party. The cake was not the actual reveal (so I did not color any of the layers pink or blue), but I did use some pink and blue sugar sprinkles to decorate the cake, which I did about 6 hours before serving the cake. That was a bad call, as the sprinkles started to bleed on the whipped cream frosting (only around the cake, not on the top for some reason) and it looked awful. I covered it up with pirouette cookies around the side of the cake, and that helped a bit. I had a group of 20 people, so I doubled the entire recipe for the cake (quadrupled the coffee/liquor).  With double the cake batter, the cake was a little unwieldy, and I don't recommend doubling the entire recipe.  I also had doubled the frosting and filling, which was unnecessary and I had enough fros

text:
Everyone raved about this cake and it tasted like a restaurant version of tiramisu!  In making it, I misread "instant coffee powder" and thought it was coffee grounds.  As I mixed grounds into a tiny bit of water (as some suggested), I realized the coffee was supposed to be finer, so I just poured the liquid through a sifter and it was fine.  I doubled the coffee & liquour as others suggested and used coffee flavored vodka rather than liquour, which was all I had, but turned out to be great, as it actually came through a bit.  I wasn't sure why everyone subbed out the mascarpone cheese, as it was only $2.99 at my grocery store, only a dollar more than cream cheese - I was very glad I went with this as it gave it the spot-on flavor.  I had excess whipping cream frosting (cake only needed about 2/3s of what I made), but I set it out for others to add on to their piece of cake if they desired.  I followed the advice of others and froze my 3 layers before stacking and that made it easy.  Fantastic recipe!

text:
OMG.... I LOVED this cake! My family is having a friendly "cake-off" competition this summer and this was my entry. Let's just say, I'm feeling confident! ;-)  

To get my bonus points, I did use a from-scratch white cake recipe (Heavenly White Cake, from this site), rather than boxed. I made a 1 1/2 batch, just to be sure I'd have enough cake and I figured if each layer was a bit thicker, that was fine by me. I used 3 nine-inch cake pans and the thickness was perfect. 

Additionally, like many other reviewers recommended, I added extra coffee liquor whenever called for (except the frosting, I left that as-is w/ 2 Tbsp), doubled the brewed coffee mixture, and doubled the instant coffee added to the cake layers. Yes, I left one layer plain/white and I made two "coffee" by adding instant coffee. I did not need to dilute the instant coffee in water as another reveiwer said. I simply folded the granules in until well incorporated. This worked great for me! 

For the filling, I used the mascarpone cheese. It's very reasonable at Trader Joe's and I felt it was best to stay true to the recipe here. (This filling was fantastic!)

Once my cakes were baked & cooled, plus my filling & frosting were made, assembly was quite easy & fun. The frosting spread so nicely. I finished off the presentation with chocolate covered espressso beans. 

This was a cake I will most definitely make again! The whole family loved it! :)

text:
Yum, yum!  This was an amazing recipe!  I did read many of the reviews and this is what I found.  I used Duncan Hines cake mix.  I used the Mascarpone cheese not the substitute.  I 4X the amount of coffee powder and used espresso powder.  I used a cold brew concentrate coffee for the brewed coffee.  I doubled all of the liqueur except in the frosting because one reviewer said that could have led to problems with the frosting in the fat to liquid ratio.  I did add some coffee powder to the frosting instead of more liqueur.  I made 2 coffee layers and one white.  I followed one reviewer's suggestion to leave the cake in the pans ( I used disposable pans) and cool in the pan on a wire rack for 15 minutes, then poke holes in the cake, add your coffee mixture and put the cakes in the pans in the freezer for 20 minutes.  This worked really well during assembling.  The cakes came out of the pans easily and stacked well.  Thank you Bettina for an amazing easy recipe!!!!

I have made this cake several times for different occasions.  BIG hit!  Here are some tweaks that I have made each time: substitute for the mascarpone - 16oz spreadable cream cheese, 1/2 c heavy cream, 5 tbsp sour cream.  Super creamy and yummy. I also double the coffee flavored liqueur (each time it is listed).  For the frosting step, I have found that I should not mix ingredients for more than 4 minutes or they begin to separate/change textures.  Last tip - make several hours (or a day) in advance and make sure to keep refrigerated.

text:
This is so good, it'd be a shame to not give this a go. Delicious, mouth-watering and personally, I found this quite easy to make! I didn't opt for the cake mix. Instead, I made my own white cake from scratch, using my all-time favourite 'Simple White Cake' recipe from this site. I used the suggestions of the reviewers and made 2 of the cakes coffee (by adding a teaspoon or 2 of instant coffee into the cake batter) and I left the other one as is. 
I'd recommend being generous with the coffee-kahlua mix when pouring them over the cakes ... it does wonders to the flavour and keeps them moist. 
I made one amendment to the recipe for the whipped cream frosting ... I stabilised the frosting. Here's how - take about 1 tablespoon of gelatin and dissolve it in about 3-4 tablespoons of warm water. Mix well so that the gelatin is dissolved completely. As soft peaks start to form while whipping the cream, add the gelatin mix into it and keep whipping the cream until stiff. Once stabilised, the cream is a dream to work with and do lovely designs with. I left mine simple and dusted it with cocoa powder and coffee beans/cacao nibs! 
Ah yes, lastly, making this about 24 hours before serving is an excellent idea 'coz that gives the cake enough time to set. And ofcourse, be generous with the cream and filling ... 'coz that's where all the magic lies! 
Thank you for this recipe!

text:
GREAT Taste, but still pretty putsy.  I have never made the original version with Lady Fingers, but I had a frustrating time with my 3 layers of white cake; the amount that baked up in the pans was approximately less than 2" high and very flimsy.... Lady Fingers are far more dense, so trying to get the cake out from the pans in one piece did NOT happen no matter how much I greased down the pans and floured them, per instructions.  I would skip the round pans, and just do square pans.  I think Tiramisu would be so much better if chefs would just focus on the TASTE not the goofy fancy ordeal it takes to make it.  If I made Tiramisu my way, it would be one cake layer and one cream layer, with chocolate shavings on top. I'm sure it would taste exactly the same, just have a slightly different texture compared to a multi-layered dessert...

text:
Made this for my birthday today. I had hoped it would not be frustrating, but it turned out to be a little more work than I expected. I cut out the coffee liquer (since my toddler will be having a slice, and I didn't want to risk it since the filling and frosting aren't cooked). First, my complaints. I did use cream cheese instead of marscapone, because it wasn't available. It was very hard to 'fold' the frosting into the filling, perhaps I didn't beat the filling enough? Either way, the filling was not very easy to spread, I think next time I make this, I'll just add some of the cream and a little more sugar into the filling and then beat it at a high speed. The frosting, however, was AMAZING, it was so easy to spread, I just hope it sets in the fridge and doesn't dissolve. I did add some cream of tartar to the frosting, just a trick I learned about whipped cream. One the frosting sets, right before serving, I'm going to add the garnish. :3 The frosting and filling were delicious, I licked the bowl.

text:
I made this as a birthday cake for my son, who had been trying to get me to make him Tiramisu for years. I never did because I had always heard it was difficult to make. Although this recipe wasn't super easy, it wasn't difficult either. I followed the recipe exactly as written, except that I doubled the liquor, "only" in the coffee, and used half Bailey's and half Kahlua there). I almost doubled the liquor everywhere because I read so many reviews that suggested this. However, I was glad I didn't when I tasted the final results. I thought it had the perfect balance as it was, I didn't want to taste the liquor...just wanted it as flavoring, and that is how it came out. This cake had a moist, delicious, and well-balanced flavor. My son said that it tasted like an "authentic" Tiramisu, he loved it...and so did everyone else! :)

This is a great cake. However, it does take some work.  I made this for a mixed group of people (coffee lovers and non coffee lovers) and I still got rave reviews. text:
Absolutly wonderful and easy! I usually make a from scrath recipe and this was much easier! As previous reviews explain, some adjustements can be made. I prefer cake that isn't soaked in liquid so I did a version without the coffee poured on the cake layers. Here my version (somewhat taste  like the mokamisu cake at rocaberry's restaurant. 1) I use the french vanilla cake mix 2) in 2 of the 3 cake layers, i added 3 tsp of instant espresso powder per cake layer. 3) for the filling, i also substituted the mascarpone for 1 pack (250g) cream cheese, 1/2 cup heavy cream and 3 tbsp sour cream, blended those ingredients then combined the sugar and kaluah. 4)i double the kaluah (coffee liqueur) in the filling and the frosting. 5) when assembling, i put 1 layer coffe cake, half the cheese filling, then a layer of french vanilla, then the rest of cheese filling, one more layer of coffee cake. After frosting the cake, i dusted it with dark cacao powder and then garnished the sides and middle of top with white and dark chocolate curls. To make chocolate curl, just melt the chocolate and then put it in a rectangular pan (ex: bread loaf pan) and refrigerate until solid but not to cold. Take out block of chocolate from it. If it got to cold, microwave 10-15 sec at a time. Curls are done by running down accross it with cheese slicer or carrot peeler. If curls are not forming, it's still too cold.  At this point, the cake sort of tastes like a moka cake, but trust me, you'll enjoy!

text:
This rating is based on origional recipe. I guess my expectations were very high after reading all the ratings on this cake. The flavor was too subtle in my opinion, especially being a Tiramisu lover. In my opinion it was labor intensive and would be easier to make a traditional Tiramisu with ladyfingers. I used Kahlua for my coffee liqueur and instant expresso. I only used a pint of heavy cream and it was enough to frost the entire cake. For the price of Marscapone cheese I felt it didn't make an impact from the outer whipped cream frosting. My guests felt the same that it was good but not outstanding. I would have to agree with others and say if you want to try this recipe definately double up on all the coffee and liqueur. I think I will try it again and double up on all the flavors and then it would might be 5 stars.

The cake was moist and delicious!  I followed advice of others and made two layers with the instant coffee. text:
This was amazing. It wasn't that easy to make, but the results were worth it. Instead of having two white cakes, I added about a fourth cup of cocoa butter to 1/3 the white cake recipe ( http://allrecipes.com/Recipe/Simple-White-Cake/Detail.aspx ) as well as dark chocolate chips.  In the next 1/3 i added 1/4 cup white chocolate chips, although I believe I could have added more. To the final 1/3 I added about a 1/3-1/2 cup of extremely dark coffee. Instead of marscapone cheese I used yogurt, as I don't have cream cheese, as well as a bit of whipped cream, which I had more than enough.  My family loved it and licked their plates. This is definetly a recipe to remember.  BTW, I'm 14, so if I can do it, so can you!

text:
Loved this recipe!!  I made it for my mom's birthday (who loves tiramisu) and everyone loved it.

I did follow some advice from posters.  I tripled the amount of coffee (and I used instant coffee intead of brewed).  I also doubled the amount of Kahlua.  I also used Duncan Hines Moist White Cake Mix and it was very light and moist.  I made 2 coffee layers and only one white one and made it all in three 8" pans b/c I only had 2 9" pans to use.

I could not make chocolate curls at all so it came out more like cocoa on top.  Not sure how you're supposed to make chocolate curls with a vegetable peeler.  I couldn't figure it out but it didn't effect the taste.  Very light and had the same taste and texture as real tiramisu. :)  A definite keeper!

text:
This cake was really enjoyed by my family and guests. Presentation was Bakery quality and not too difficult to make. I used French Vanilla Kahluha and Peet's Major Dickason's Blend coffee. WOW! What a flavor together! I doubled the main flavors and made chocolate whipped cream (from what remained after frosting the cake of the regular frosting). I used the chocolate whipped cream in a pastry bag with a large star tip and decorated the top of the cake as well as along the bottom. I shaved the best 60% bittersweet chocolate I could find on the top of the cake and chilled it for a full day before serving it. To my surprise it was even better after the third day (family couldn't finish it because it is quite rich and they wanted it for breakfast with MORE coffee:). I will make this again, but double the filling as it is sooo good. Very impressive recipe, and as the flavors had more time to blend I swear the "boxed cake" taste was not detectable. It was a little more expensive to make, but beats the heck out of most cakes you can buy. One final note, some of my guests actually said they enjoyed the cake more than real Tiramisu because they liked having the  traditional flavor without raw eggs in the recipe. This cake is definately worth the time to make!

text:
I made this cake a couple of years ago for my daughter's 17th birthday and now it has become "The Birthday Cake" for both of my children. I use more expresso and also use coffee syrup flavoring.
Want to update this rating. The last couple of  times I made this it has fallen apart. The reason for this is the layers were not level. Be sure to trim off the top of the cakes if they do not bake flat. With all the fillings you all a lot of moisture to the cake and it  will fall apart if it the cake surface is not flat. Next time I make the cake I will be sure to take care of this. I still highly recommend this recipe. Yummy!

For anyone having trouble getting their cream to whip and thicken, make sure you are NOT using "ultra pasteurized" heavy cream. It will not thicken when whipped.  I learned the hard way several years ago.

This was a real hit at my office party.  There was none left for me to take home:(
I did change a couple of things.  I made only two layers, added more coffee, no liquer, and did not have marscopone cheese so I used a cheater/cheaper version with cream cheese, cool whip, and powdered sugar.  The only reason I am giving it 4 instead of 5 is because of the icing.  It had very little flavor and adding the coffee turned it a dingy color as opposed to white.  I used heavy whipping cream and finally got it stiff enough.  I think the next time, I will just double the good stuff in the middle and use that for the icing as well.  This was my first recipe from here and I consider it a success.  I plan to make it for our Christmas party, by request, of course.

text:
Awesome cake. I made this for my sister b-day. Few things to note. I made it in 9 3/4" pans so I ended up having to make two white cakes (betty crocker) to make it large enough (doubled the recipe). Yep I goofed, but mostly I didn't have 9" pans.  Also got bad advice on what confection sugar  was (thanks grandma) so I used icing sugar.   Required a lot more icing sugar to thicken the forsting up but worked like a charm about 4 times as much.  Used cocoa powder to dust & white chocolate shavings.  Wasn't hard to do, tasted awesome, served about 20 people (generous sized pieces, because I made 2 full white cakes instead of 1) and the cake was 10-12" high when finished. The hight of the cake was later reduced when after being fully baked & iced & decorated it fell off of the table & on to the floor when I went to put in a pan for transport.  Luckily the frosting was so light and fluffy it obsorbed the impact & the cake was untouched undeneath. I refrosted, redecorated & gave it to her. We all ate it, it was a big hit. Either that or they all felt sorry for me. :o)  Seriously though, I would attempt this again, & I'd make it in the 9 3?4" pans, with the icing sugar & the two boxes of white cake. But I may opt not to drop it next time. Like everyone else I used extra Kaluah at every part. Pictures of the cake splattered and finshed will be posted so you may all see & hopefully get a laugh.

text:
Thank you Bettina for the inspiration ... my new Italian Poke Cake! Had little to work with in my kitchen so I promise next time to use the marscapone. This was SO quick and good. Made a 9 inch white Jiffy cake mix as directed on box and added 1 t. coffee crystals, 1 T. Kahlua, and 1/4 c. mayonnaise (keeps it moist). Bake 20 min., poke holes and carefully pour 1/4 c. strong coffee and 1 T. Kahlua over cake. Refrigerate while you mix up 1/2 pkg Vanilla instant pudding with 1 c. milk, 1 T. Kalua, 1/4 c. sour cream and spread over cake. Back into refrigerator. At serving time, slice and decorate each piece with spray whipped cream and cocoa powder (or grated Hershey Bar). This was a 5 star recipe for method, ease,  swapability of ingredients and my guests were licking their plates!
